    <li> Great toothbrush !! My teeth feel very clean. Operates quietly.</li>
    <li> Gets the job done!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have been a user of electric toothbrushes for the past 18 years.  I started out with Interplak and used that for almost two years, until the battery corroded.  I replaced that first electric with another from the same brand.  Eventually, the Sonicare came out and I switched to that brand.  That Sonicare lasted a very long time.  Sometime around late 2005, I bought my first Oral-B.  The Oral-B was one of their mid-end models and it also lasted a number of years.  The nickel-cadmium rechargeable batteries were still working fine, but the charging base got damaged during a move.  I replaced that one with a cheap model, also an Oral-B.  This cheap model will only hold its charge for about 3 brushing sessions before you notice a significant performance decrease and the unit would need to be fully recharged.  As they say, you do get what you pay for.  There are times when you travel and have to take the brush with you.  It  would be nice to have something that will hold a longer charge.  So, I bought this one.  This one is much better than the previous Oral-B.  It uses the same model of brush head but this model cleans more aggressively than the previous one.  So, here we are, my sixth electric toothbrush in 18-19 years of use.  Of the six models, I would say that the only ones that I did not like were the low-end Oral-B and the first Interplak.  All the rest were good at what they were supposed to do.  You do not need to spend 100+ dollars on a top-model like the Sonicare to get good results.  I have found that the key to getting good performance is to replace the brush head often.  Get the name brand brush head if you can.  The brush heads on the Sonicare tend to last longer than the ones on the Oral-B, but they are also typically more expensive.  It is your choice.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I can easily recommend this model, the Oral-B Precision 1000, to anybody who wants to use an electric toothbrush.  Spending more money will not necessarily clean your teeth better, in my experience.  What you give up is more features, like UV sterilizing and perhaps additional cleaning modes (like a gentle cycle on your washing machine, some brushes have a mode for delicate users).  My advice when it comes to electric toothbrushes is to avoid the low-end and the high-end.  somewhere in the middle is the sweet spot.  Get a model that uses the same brush heads as the higher-end models and you will get the same cleaning performance.ur teeth better, in my experience.  What you give up is more features, like UV sterilizing and perhaps additional cleaning modes (like a gentle cycle on your washing machine, some brushes have a mode for delicate users).  My advice when it comes to electric toothbrushes is to avoid the low-end and the high-end.  somewhere in the middle is the sweet spot.  Get a model that uses the same brush heads as the higher-end models and you will get the same cleaning performance.</li>

    <li> If you&#x27;re an average American, high-end electric toothbrushes and water picks have always been things you saw in movies on television in the bathrooms of the rich-the people who had good things that you didn&#x27;t have.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Oral-b Professional Care 1000 (we&#x27;ll call it, \\&quot;the PC 1000\\&quot;) Electric Toothbrush helps to rectify that; it offers you champaign dental hygiene on something nearer to a beer budget; replacing the manual toothbrush&#x27;s large, dense pack of bristles with a small, circular head that is better suited to accessing each tooth&#x27;s surface and removing food particles at the gumline where the worst of the nasty, irreversible damage happens.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Using different technologies and approaches, Oral-b&#x27;s high-end toothbrushes like the PC 1000 improve your oral hygiene not only by having a stronger action than the cheap competition (including its own low-cost vibrating toothbrushes), but by encouraging you to change your brushing habits to optimize tooth cleaning and gum health.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Brushing with it is such a different experience from using any ordinary, manual toothbrush, that just reading the instruction-sheet can leave you standing there staring as you wonder about the brushing habits you&#x27;ve had for a lifetime. Using it properly involves big changes in the way you do things.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The first change is that brushing with the Oral-b PC 1000 is counterintuitive: the brush does all the work. The PC 1000&#x60;s head combines a rapid vibrating motion with a rotating action; you use it not by vigorously scrubbing back and forth against the wall of your closed teeth, but by slowly running the brush first over your gums and then over and around each tooth individually. This provides a different and much more thorough cleaning than the one that manual toothbrushes provide.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also unlike manual toothbrushes, the PC 1000, helps to keep you honest and following the advice of dental care professionals by automatically reminding you to give each quarter of your mouth equal attention for a total of two minutes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Every thirty seconds, a timer in the brush causes the brush to &#x60;stutter&#x27; in several pulses that tells you to go on to the next section of your teeth and gums, if you&#x27;re interrupted, you can turn the brush off and it will continue the cleaning program from where it left off so long as it isn&#x27;t turned off for more than thirty seconds at a time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That&#x27;s what it does and how it does it. Oral-b claims that using the PC 1000 remove double the amount of plaque that a manual toothbrush can and that using it for fourteen days will help arrest or even partially reverse the progress of gingivitis. I can&#x27;t tell whether this is true or not without consulting a dentist. I do know that I have brushed with it and felt it loosen and remove firmer food particles from between my teeth by brushing alone and that is just scary-as in scary good performance.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all, I&#x27;m impressed with the Oral-b Professional Care 1000. It is simple to charge (plug in charging stand, put toothbrush on it) and, when used properly, it changes not only how you brush but your entire attitude towards brushing; while the cost of it is not much more than what you would pay for not too many of Oral-b&#x27;s own vibrating manual toothbrushes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I like it. I wish they had made them at this price many years and many dental complications ago.total of two minutes. That&#x27;s what it does and how it does it. Oral-b claims that using the PC 1000 remove double the amount of plaque that a manual toothbrush can and that using it for fourteen days will help arrest or even partially reverse the progress of gingivitis. It is to run water over the brush and tip of the brush holder with the brush operating. Once clean, I remove the brush and run water over it and the tip of the brush holder, with the brush holder momentarily running.  This cleanses both the brush and brush holder shaft seal.  Once rinsed, I dry the brush and brush holder tip with a towel, momentarily running the brush holder as I wipe it dry.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Oral B-1000 Professional electric toothbrush is an excellent, quality product.     <li> Oral-B has a number of brushes available - the Sonic, Vitality, the Professional Care family (which comprises the 1000 and 3000), and the Professional Care SmartSeries (4000 and 5000). The Oral-B 1000 is the entry level of the Professional Care series.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In my usage of the Vitality and the Oral-B 1000, the Oral-B 1000 stands at the minimum level of functionality to make an electric toothbrush viable.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For example, the Vitality does not have a quadrant timer (it beeps only at the end of the 2-minute cycle), is rated at only 7600 oscillations per second, and does not have battery charging indicators.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The brushes in the Professional Care series on the other hand add quadrant timers, and are rated both at 8800 oscillations per second and at 40,000 pulsations per second.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As you go higher in the Professional Care family you get multiple brush modes (daily clean, sensitive, polish, deep clean), pressure sensors, and even wireless displays.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, the brush is simply wonderful. I&#x27;ve tried the pro white, precision clean, and dual clean brush heads, and I&#x27;m simply thrilled with each, though the dual clean head is my favorite.     <li> I searched online for the best electronic toothbrush.  It turns out, the style of this toothbrush has been found by Cochrane to be the only type of electronic toothbrush that outperforms manual toothbrushes when used as directed. Cochrane does meta-analyses and they are very conservative, which means that when they say something, it is pretty much true.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I don&#x27;t completely agree with their methodology -- one benefit of using electronic toothbrushes is that people spend more time brushing their teeth with electronic toothbrushes than with manual toothbrushes, so there&#x27;s a decent chance that other electronic toothbrushes might, in the real world, outperform manual toothbrushes.  However, their meta-analysis was toothbrushes, used as directed, and with that context, I believe them.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Independent of my prompting, my dentist also recommended this very toothbrush, reinforcing my belief in its goodness.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The one annoyance is that the internals of the toothbrush drain down, which creates a gunky toothpastey sludge at the base of the charger.     <li> I&#x27;ll have to admit this is my first Oral-b ever since I started using an electric toothbrush and I am completely loving it! I decided on an Oral-b when my Sonicare started to give me trouble after 9 faithful years of use. Don&#x27;t get me wrong this doesn&#x27;t mean that Oral-b is better than Sonicare, it just means I prefer the Oral-b more. After using the Oral-b for a week I can honestly say it beats the Sonicare (the Elite/Essence model) in 2 key areas, its precision and the maintenance. The Oral-b&#x27;s head is specifically designed to be round and small allowing users to clean each individual tooth while the structural design allow for simple and easy clean up. All you have to do to clean the unit is pull the head attachment off, rinse with water, and wipe clean with a towel or napkin. My old Sonicare, Elite model not flexcare, replacement heads was twisted on similar to a cup. This was extremely painful to clean because I would have to twist the head off, pop out the brush head, clean the round base, and then clean the handle mouth. If I didn&#x27;t do this after each use the tooth paste drip off while brushing will seep inside the brush unit and the handle unit turning into mold. Completely unsanitary! Even after purchasing the SonicSeal, which I highly suggest to anyone who has the Elite/Essence model, mold would still build up at the bottom of the SonicSeal/Sonicare handle without proper cleaning. I also didn&#x27;t feel like I had much precision cleaning my teeth because the brush head is long and wide. I always had to awkwardly position the brush to clean the inside of my teeth, the outer portion is really easy though.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Beside these 2 factors, I think both toothbrush does a great job at cleaning your teeth, one just requires more work. I never really bought into the whole Oral-b vs. Sonicare debate because technically any electric toothbrush is better than a manual one. I get the same squeaky clean fresh feeling after I brush using either the Oral-b or Sonicare. Like I mentioned earlier, neither toothbrush is better than the other at cleaning your teeth, it&#x27;s just the Oral-b gives you better precision and is easier to maintain.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Some miscellaneous difference between the Oral-b and Sonicare (Elite model):&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. The Oral-b works by oscillating (moving side by side), so there is no need to brush when its on just move it tooth to tooth. The Sonicare uses sonic technology by vibrating, so brushing is required when the unit is on or it won&#x27;t clean at all just vibrates based on my experiences.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2. The Oral-b has a quadrant timer just like the Sonicare. They will both pause after each 30 seconds indicating when to change quadrant, but unlike the Sonicare which stops automatically after 2 mins the Oral-b will continue on until prompted by the user to stop. I love this because I brush for 3 mins not 2.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3. The charge indicator is different for both units. The Sonicare will blink green when charging and stay green when fully charged until removed from the charging base. The Oral-b will blink green when charging and stop blinking when fully charged. I had to pull out the manual to make sure the Oral-b was fully charged and working. I thought it malfunctioned because the light stayed off.I mentioned earlier, neither toothbrush is better than the other at cleaning your teeth, it&#x27;s just the Oral-b gives you better precision and is easier to maintain.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Some miscellaneous difference between the Oral-b and Sonicare (Elite model):&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. The Oral-b works by oscillating (moving side by side), so there is no need to brush when its on just move it tooth to tooth. The Sonicare uses sonic technology by vibrating, so brushing is required when the unit is on or it won&#x27;t clean at all just vibrates based on my experiences.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2. The Oral-b has a quadrant timer just like the Sonicare. They will both pause after each 30 seconds indicating when to change quadrant, but unlike the Sonicare which stops automatically after 2 mins the Oral-b will continue on until prompted by the user to stop. I love this because I brush for 3 mins not 2.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3. The charge indicator is different for both units. The Sonicare will blink green when charging and stay green when fully charged until removed from the charging base. The Oral-b will blink green when charging and stop blinking when fully charged. I had to pull out the manual to make sure the Oral-b was fully charged and working. I thought it malfunctioned because the light stayed off.</li>

    <li> For many years I&#x27;ve used the Oral B budget version (appx. $20) of their pro electric toothbrush and loved it. The strong motor and small head just works so much better than most other brand of electric toothbrushes and infinitely more cleaner than using a manual brush. Since the design elements on the budget versions are similar to the pro versions and uses the same toothbrush head, I thought the budget Oral B electric toothbrush was just as good as the more expensive Oral-B Pros.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;However, when I got an Oral-B 1000 Pro Care Electric Toothbrush, the differences were very noticeable! I felt like I went from a classy compact car to a luxurious full-size premier sedan! The motor on the Oral-B 1000 is much more refined. The body is taller and more slender. It makes for a much better brushing experience.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One of my unexpected pleasures of the Oral-B 1000 Pro toothbrush is the built in timers. One goes off once every 20 seconds to remind you to move onto the next section of your teeth. Then the 2-minute warning saying you&#x27;ve completed the recommended minimum time to brush your teeth. Nice! One kept me from working too fast, the other reminded me that it&#x27;s time to finish up.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I really like the small round toothbrush head. It reaches to the back teeth, gets into tight corners, and is able to give a good scrub in every dental nook and cranny. The blue bands fade over time to remind you to replace the toothbrush head after a while. (Con: I&#x27;m not fond on how expensive the toothbrush head replacements are - yikes!) Surely, the round brush head give me the best clean. No other toothbrush shape comes close.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I&#x27;m loving the Oral-B 1000. It&#x27;s an excellent toothbrush and a pleasure to use. It makes for a better tooth-brushing experience for me. I&#x27;ll never go back if I can help it.</li>
    <li> Electric brushes can be a good thing - there is quite a bit more cleaning action going on because the automatic brush strokes are way faster than your hand can perform so you will always get better cleaning.  Also, I have found the rotating action of the head allows you to position it in hard-to-reach areas and then just allow it to do its work, whereas it&#x27;s much less likely to get sufficient cleaning action manually - especially if, like me, you still have some wisdom teeth left and you are concerned about keeping them from decaying.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I also am an &#x27;over-brusher&#x27;, so I tend to brush too long and too vigorously, and have caused some unneccessary gum receding and enamel damage.  That&#x27;s one caution I would make with the electric toothbrushes - you get plenty of brushing action and &#x27;more&#x27; is not necessarily better.  Sometimes a light brushing and some flossing or toothpick action would serve you better than long, intense brushing.  This brush has a light pause built into it to let you know you are brushing too hard - probably a good thing for those of us so interest in dental hygiene that we will buy these gizmos.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One reason I got interested in the electronic toothbrushes, is I tend to brush up and down too hard and I was causing both irritation and receding in a couple areas of my gums and a friend mentioned that her dentist said the rotary-action of these brushes can help correct that a bit - sure enough, I found I stopped making my gum sore every time I brushed, plus brushing was so much more enjoyable in general.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I started a few years back with the cell-type battery powered brushes, but they always tended to die on me in a few months, so about a year and a half ago, I went to Oral-B&#x27;s cheapest re-chargeable  model.  I had absolutely no problems with it.  When I went to the dentist recently after not having gone for over twenty years, they seemed to think my teeth were in outstanding shape, except for the fact that I was over-brushing.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The difference in the smooth-running feel of this nicer tooth-brush versus the cheaper Oral-B one is pretty noticeable - the same level of difference I noticed when going from the cell-type battery brushes to my first Oral-B rechargeable one.  Both rechargeable models have the built-in &#x27;three big pauses&#x27; signal to let you know you have brushed for a full two minutes, however, I am re-thinking whether I need to follow the 2-minute recommendation every time I brush, since over-brushing is the greatest bane my teeth have.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A couple recommendations:  This brush will accomodate the &#x27;dual-action&#x27; heads, and once I tried those, going back to the single action was really lame.  Dual-action rocks.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also, in case you don&#x27;t know, always take the head off of the brush, rinse well, and leave it off to dry, just putting back on the next time you brush.  This should keep any bacteria from growing in the brush head.  If you still notice a smell of bacteria, or just want to make sure to get it extra clean, use very hot water when rinsing or even have a spray bottle of strong alcohol available to spray into the bottom of the brush head before you lay it down to dry out.  I noticed a change in brushing heads was called for in anywhere from three to six months, not because the bristles wear down, but the head becomes slightly looser and it would sort of start pinching my gum or tongue a bit as my skin could get slightly caught between the loose plastic.  The miser in me wants to continue until the head simply falls apart, but it&#x27;s much better to just break down and get a new one at that point, thereby avoiding the discomfort, and getting back to enjoying the luxury of a nice electronic toothbrush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also, I followed the instructions in the package of my last rechargeable to allow the battery to completely drain every three months or so.  This is a bit of a challenge, because the brush turns off by itself, so even though you leave it off the charger, once it&#x27;s worn down a bit, it will stop and turn off, even though it is not completely drained.  I found that simply hitting the &#x27;on&#x27; button as many times as I could as I went by, I was able to get it down to truly dead, but it generally requires using the bush manually for a day or so, until it is completely dead and then you can charge it back up.  I did this because I wanted my brush to last as long as possible and will do it with this new one too.  I&#x27;m assuming it does something like clear the memory on the battery when you allow it to go completely dead.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Two of my personal dental hygiene recommendations:  Be a bit careful about using baking soda or toothpastes with strong abrasives if you are an &#x27;over-brusher&#x27; which can cause even more worn enamel.  Also, &#x27;tartar control&#x27; products are highly under-rated in my opinion.  I personally feel the chemicals in pastes and rinses that say &#x27;tartar-control&#x27; really work, although I will admit, my dentist doesn&#x27;t seem one bit impressed with them.  Still, I used these products faithfully for the 20 years I had no professional dental care, and I had hardly any tartar build-up when I got my teeth cleaned, whereas previously, I did not use the products, and went to the dentist every 6 months and they seemed to find a reasonable amount of tartar to scrape off each time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Anyway, this is a wonderful product that makes an annoying daily-plus chore downright enjoyable and keeps your teeth looking and chewing nicely.  Just don&#x27;t over-brush.f, even though it is not completely drained.  I found that simply hitting the &#x27;on&#x27; button as many times as I could as I went by, I was able to get it down to truly dead, but it generally requires using the bush manually for a day or so, until it is completely dead and then you can charge it back up.  I did this because I wanted my brush to last as long as possible and will do it with this new one too.  I&#x27;m assuming it does something like clear the memory on the battery when you allow it to go completely dead.    Two of my personal dental hygiene recommendations:  Be a bit careful about using baking soda or toothpastes with strong abrasives if you are an &#x27;over-brusher&#x27; which can cause even more worn enamel.  Also, &#x27;tartar control&#x27; products are highly under-rated in my opinion.  I personally feel the chemicals in pastes and rinses that say &#x27;tartar-control&#x27; really work, although I will admit, my dentist doesn&#x27;t seem one bit impressed with them.  Still, I used these products faithfully for the 20 years I had no professional dental care, and I had hardly any tartar build-up when I got my teeth cleaned, whereas previously, I did not use the products, and went to the dentist every 6 months and they seemed to find a reasonable amount of tartar to scrape off each time.    Anyway, this is a wonderful product that makes an annoying daily-plus chore downright enjoyable and keeps your teeth looking and chewing nicely.  Just don&#x27;t over-brush.</li>

This just isn&#x27;t possible with this head so I have to continually inhale gently to keep spit from coming out through the toothbrush head. I&#x27;ve gotten used to it but the truth is I still sometimes end up with toothpaste spit down the front of me, a problem I&#x27;ve never had with any other toothbrush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The only other complaint is the battery. The first one I had went dead within about a month. I sent it in for repair and they replaced the battery. It&#x27;s been about 5 months since then and it seems to be fine now. Still, all of these rechargeable batteries have the same problem: they never last as long as they are supposed to. To prolong the life of the battery I would strongly recommend not putting it on the charger after every use. Wait until the low battery light flashes. I get about 15 brushes per charge. That&#x27;s a pretty reasonable number but unless I&#x27;m very lucky, it won&#x27;t take long before the charge starts dropping off fast.</li>

At the urging of the professionals, acquired the Oral-B and have reduced the staining by at least 90%.  The only down side is the induction recharging, which requires a good 15 to 17 hours for full recharge. So, if the low battery shows at night and set to recharge, the unit will not be fully recharged until the following evening. A charge lasts about a week, used twice a day, consistent w/ the informational pamphlet. But if more than one person uses it, that really cuts down the use time, and that&#x27;s where the overly long recharge period is an issue. \\&quot;Constant\\&quot; recharge would likely solve the issue, but at the cost of reducing the life of the battery itself. Yes, the induction system has no exposed contacts, looks \\&quot;neat\\&quot;, etc., but sacrifices efficient recharge time (maybe that&#x27;s why these are also available as 2-unit packs). Overall, the Oral-B has done wonders for the teeth, but the excessive recharge time gets the product 4 stars, not 5.</li>

So I end up having to hit those manually with my old Cybersonic head. Bummer. I&#x27;ve had to readjust how I brush my inner bottom fronts too. But other than that, I&#x27;m pretty happy with my purchase. Especially since I got everything so cheap!iving me nuts, but I found a small bait-and-tackle type case at Daiso for $1.50 that fits everything perfectly (I&#x27;ll try to  post a pic).     <li> **EDIT March 2014**&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After one and a half years, the battery seems to be getting worse over time. Despite following the charging instructions and recommendations provided by the manufacturer, there seems to be a disconnect between the battery indicating \\&quot;low\\&quot; vs. the battery depletion time. After the last few charging cycles, I have noticed that the unit will not indicate that the battery is low and needs to be recharged. However, the next brushing cycle will abruptly end after about a minute and THEN indicates that the battery is low and must be charged. Pressing the power button will not turn the unit back on. Hence, I now have to feel out when the battery may be getting low or just charge it every day, rather than once a week or when the unit indicates a low battery. Technically, it is still under warranty, but the shipping cost is on me, making it more worthwhile to just continue using the product as-is or buy a newer model.     <li> Update: I never got back to this but two of us bought one of these on the basis of a rebate and neither of us ever received the rebate. The battery is now starting to need to be recharged noticeably more often now, so expect the life of one of these to last 3-4 years, which might not be as long as you expected it to last. I have a personal policy that when I get screwed over on a rebate, I do my best to not buy items from the same company again. While it might be difficult to avoid all Proctor and Gamble products, I will avoid Oral B products from now on, just as I avoid medicines from Abbott Pharmaceuticals after they screwed me over on a rebate for a blood glucose monitor. I figure that they&#x27;ll lose a lot more money on me than they gained by screwing me on a rebate.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This electric toothbrush works very well. No gimmicks, it just works. It&#x27;s the one recommended to me by my dental hygienist.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Every 30 seconds for the 2-minute standard timing for brushing your teeth, it vibrates differently to let you now it&#x27;s time to move on to the next quadrant in your mouth. You can stop the brush at that point to add more toothpaste (I use baking soda myself) and press it again. It remembers where you are in the time cycle unless you leave it off for a couple of minutes, when it will reset itself.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It takes a long time to charge up fully the first time, but that&#x27;s a good thing since the charger is not forcing a lot of current into the battery. You can store it on the charging base or elsewhere. It will need another charge in about a week. Every several months you should completely discharge the battery then recharge it according to the instructions. You may find that not keeping it on the charging base and just charging it when it runs down may provide a longer battery life.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The battery appears to not be replaceable, but you can remove it when it&#x27;s time to dispose of the product so you can recycle it properly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This product came with a plastic travel case, which I may use infrequently, but it&#x27;s nice to have something to protect it. There are generic brush heads available. I haven&#x27;t tried any of these yet, but I have read that some generic brush heads do not last and break. Some work, others don&#x27;t, and you can have a mix of these in a batch if you buy them from online auction sites. If you buy them from Amazon, you can return them if you find them to be defective or are otherwise not satisfied.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The brushes have some bristles with a tint that fades over time to let you know when it&#x27;s time to replace it. I think it&#x27;s more of a marketing tool to get you to buy replacement heads more often, but you can use that as a reminder if you prefer. I will replace mine when it feels too soft.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You can buy a few different types of brush heads for this device. The user guide shows which ones you can buy and what each one&#x27;s purpose is.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The brush heads have a colored ring between the head and handle so you can tell one from another if more than two people in a household use the same product. The downside is that when you buy the product, you have no way of knowing which color of ring is in the package. We bought two of them and fortunately they had different colors to tell them apart. The replacement heads, if you buy them in a multi-pack, have different colored rings, so if you buy one of those packs when you buy the product, you will probably have several colors to choose from. Alternatively, you would color one ring with fingernail polish and let it dry before putting it on a brush head, or just use some colored tape around one or more of them in your bathroom. You could even make a label for each handle with the user&#x27;s name on it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, this is much better than the inexpensive ones I&#x27;ve had in the past. I will definitely brush my teeth more often now that it&#x27;s so easy to do. Easy to do? How hard can it be to brush your teeth with a regular toothbrush?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br/&gt;You have to try one of these to understand. I tend to brush too quickly, and this device helps me time how long I brush in each quarter of my mouth. Sure, I could set a timer and keep an eye on it, switching to different parts of my mouth as the timer counts down, but this is very convenient. It also probably does a better job without brushing too hard.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Oral B (made by Braun) makes different models that use the same brush heads. This model is great. I haven&#x27;t tried the others, but they are likely well made, like other products I&#x27;ve had made by Braun.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you found this review helpful, please click the YES button below this review.
